### google/gemini-2.5-flash — `P_L_TRIZ_OFF`
1. **IDENTIFY THE CHALLENGE.**
The core technical trade-off is between **precision of solder application/heating** and **production speed**. To solder very thin gold chains, micro-doses of solder are needed, and heating must be localized to avoid damaging the delicate chain. This precision typically slows down the process. Conversely, achieving high production rates (tens to hundreds of meters per day) usually requires faster, less precise methods that would be detrimental to thin chains. The conflict is that the process needs to be both extremely precise (for micro-doses and localized heating) and extremely fast (for high throughput).

2. **SEARCH FOR RESOURCES.**
*   **Gold chain material:** Gold is an excellent electrical conductor and has a relatively low melting point compared to other metals.
*   **Solder material:** Typically a gold alloy with a lower melting point than the chain itself.
*   **Micro-doses:** Small, pre-formed solder spheres or paste.
*   **Environment:** Air, inert gas.
*   **By-products:** Heat, potentially small amounts of vaporized solder/flux.
*   **Empty space:** The small gaps between chain links.
*   **Properties of materials:** Surface tension of molten solder, electrical resistance of the gold links.

3. **APPLY DESIGN TACTICS.**
The primary tactic to apply here is **Segmentation** (dividing an object into independent parts) combined with **Local Quality** (making different parts of an object perform different functions or be in different conditions).
*   **Segmentation:** Instead of trying to heat the entire chain or even large sections, we need to segment the heating process to individual links or even specific points on a link.
*   **Local Quality:** The heating needs to be localized to the joint, and the solder application needs to be localized to the gap. The chain itself should remain cool, while the joint area is heated.

A secondary tactic is **Pneumatic or Hydraulic Structures** (using gas or liquid for function) for solder removal, and **Self-Service** (an object serves itself) for precise solder placement.

4. **RESOLVE, DON'T TRADE OFF.**
The solution involves using the chain's inherent electrical conductivity for highly localized heating and leveraging surface tension for precise solder placement and excess removal.

The chain links themselves can be used as resistive heating elements. By passing a precisely controlled, very short pulse of electrical current directly through the two links to be joined, only the contact points and immediate vicinity will heat up rapidly due to electrical resistance. This provides highly localized heating without affecting the rest of the chain.

For solder application, pre-formed micro-solder spheres (or a precisely dispensed micro-drop of solder paste) can be placed at the joint. The molten solder, due to surface tension, will naturally flow into the gap between the heated links. Any excess solder can be removed by a precisely directed, very short burst of inert gas (e.g., argon) or by a vacuum nozzle immediately after the solder melts and flows, while it's still molten. The gas jet or vacuum can be precisely controlled to only affect the excess, not the joint itself. This allows for rapid, precise, and localized heating and solder management, enabling high throughput.

5. **MAXIMIZE VALUE.**
This approach uses the existing material (gold chain) as the heating element, minimizing added components. It leverages natural phenomena (electrical resistance, surface tension) for precision. The gas jet/vacuum for excess removal is a simple, fast, and non-contact method.

FINAL SOLUTION:
A specialized machine feeds the ultra-thin gold chain continuously. As each link joint reaches a soldering station, a tiny, pre-measured sphere of gold solder is precisely placed into the gap between the two links. Two miniature, conductive contacts then briefly touch the links on either side of the joint. A precisely controlled, very short pulse of electric current is passed directly through these two links. The electrical resistance of the gold at the contact points rapidly heats only the immediate joint area, melting the solder sphere. Due to surface tension, the molten solder is drawn perfectly into the tiny gap, forming a strong bond. Immediately after, a focused micro-jet of inert gas or a tiny vacuum nozzle removes any minuscule excess solder before it solidifies. The chain then advances to the next joint, allowing for continuous, high-speed production.

This method works because it uses the gold chain itself as a resistive heater, concentrating heat only where it's needed for a fraction of a second. The inherent properties of molten solder, like surface tension, ensure it flows precisely into the joint. The gas jet or vacuum provides a non-contact, rapid way to clean up any excess, preventing damage to the delicate chain while maintaining high throughput.

    *   **Characteristic Worsens:** Applying this localized heat risks overheating and damaging the extremely thin gold links and the integrity of the entire chain. (Parameter: Durability, Reliability, Shape)

3.  **APPLY INVENTIVE PRINCIPLES.**

    *   **Principle 3: Local Quality:** Change an object's structure from uniform to non-uniform, or an external environment from uniform to non-uniform. Make each part of an object fulfill a different function.
    *   **Principle 10: Preliminary Action:** Perform the required change (or part of it) in advance.
    *   **Principle 18: Mechanical Vibration:** Use oscillations.
    *   **Principle 28: Mechanics Substitution:** Replace a mechanical means with an optical, acoustic, or thermal field.

    *   **Principle 35: Parameter Changes:** Change the physical state of an object (e.g., gas, liquid, solid). Change the concentration or consistency. Change the degree of flexibility. Change the temperature.

The high thermal conductivity of gold helps distribute the heat quickly, ensuring a strong bond without overheating. Any excess solder can be removed by a gentle ultrasonic cleaning process, which vibrates the chain in a cleaning solution, dislodging unwanted solder without harming the links. This method allows for the soldering of tens to hundreds of meters of chain per day, maintaining the chain's integrity and appearance.

### openai/gpt-4o — `P_S_TRIZ_OFF`
To solder very thin and ultra-thin gold chains, a precise and controlled method is required. First, use a micro-dispenser to apply a tiny amount of gold solder paste to the gaps between the links. This paste should have a melting point slightly lower than that of the chain to prevent damage. Next, employ a focused laser beam to heat the solder paste. The laser should be finely tuned to target only the solder paste, ensuring that the heat does not spread to the rest of the chain. This localized heating will melt the solder, creating a strong bond between the links. After soldering, use a gentle ultrasonic cleaning process to remove any excess solder. This method ensures that the chain remains intact and undamaged while achieving a high-quality solder joint.

FINAL SOLUTION:
To solder ultra-thin gold chains, start by using a micro-dispenser to apply a small amount of gold solder paste to the gaps between the links. The solder paste should have a lower melting point than the chain to avoid damage. Then, use a focused laser beam to heat the solder paste precisely. The laser should be adjusted to target only the solder paste, ensuring that the heat does not affect the rest of the chain. This localized heating will melt the solder, creating a strong bond between the links. After soldering, employ a gentle ultrasonic cleaning process to remove any excess solder. This approach allows for precise soldering of the chain without causing harm, ensuring a high-quality and durable connection between the links.

### openai/gpt-4o — `P_S_TRIZ_ON`
To solder the links of ultra-thin gold chains efficiently, a precision-focused approach is necessary. First, employ a micro-dispensing system that can accurately deposit tiny amounts of solder paste directly into the gaps between the chain links. This system should be equipped with a high-resolution camera and software to ensure precise placement. Next, use a focused infrared laser to heat the solder paste. The laser should be finely tuned to target only the solder without affecting the surrounding gold, which can be achieved by adjusting the wavelength and intensity to match the absorption characteristics of the solder material. Finally, to remove any excess solder, a gentle ultrasonic cleaning process can be applied. This process uses high-frequency sound waves to dislodge and remove excess material without damaging the delicate chain.

FINAL SOLUTION:
The solution involves a three-step process to solder ultra-thin gold chains. First, a micro-dispensing system accurately deposits tiny amounts of solder paste into the gaps between the chain links. This system uses a high-resolution camera and software to ensure precise placement. Next, a focused infrared laser heats the solder paste. The laser is finely tuned to target only the solder, avoiding damage to the surrounding gold by adjusting the wavelength and intensity to match the solder's absorption characteristics. Finally, any excess solder is removed using a gentle ultrasonic cleaning process. This process employs high-frequency sound waves to dislodge and remove excess material without harming the delicate chain. This method ensures efficient soldering of ultra-thin gold chains while maintaining their integrity and appearance.
